## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling / materials science
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting mechanical stress from strain and temperature, which is a classic constitutive modeling problem in materials science. Stress typically depends on strain through elastic/plastic hardening laws and on temperature through thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic regime)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic strain hardening)
- Linear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - T) (elastic modulus decreasing linearly with temperature)
- Johnson-Cook simplified: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (Arrhenius-type temperature dependence)
- Voce hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook full thermal term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - ((T - c3) * c4)**c5) (homologous temperature softening)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic/hyperelastic)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * epsilon**c2)**(-1) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Arrhenius-type constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T**(-1)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Ludwik model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal effect)
- Bilinear model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (linear interaction model)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T**(-1))) (Sellars-Tegart / Zener-Hollomon type)
- Swift hardening with softening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (1 - c3 * T) (Swift law with linear thermal term)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening (concave-down stress-strain curve) → Power-law epsilon**c with 0<c<1, or saturating forms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening (stress decreases with temperature) → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (T_melt - T)**c or exp(-c*T)
- Thermally activated processes (creep, diffusion) → Arrhenius factor exp(c * T**(-1)) indicating activation energy dependence
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Additive decomposition: sigma = c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 where c0 represents yield stress
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → Product form c0*(c1 - c2*T)*epsilon where the modulus is a linear function of T
- Strain-temperature coupling → Exponent or prefactor that depends on T, e.g., epsilon**(c0 + c1*T), indicating temperature changes the hardening rate
- Saturation stress at large strains → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or rational form epsilon/(epsilon + c) approaching a plateau
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as (T - T_ref)*c0 or normalized form, reflecting distance from reference/melting temperature

## Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
$$7.774\epsilon^3 + 55.124\epsilon^{0.266}\exp\left(\frac{-52.487}{8.314T}\right) + 3.805\epsilon\sin(T - 276.439)$$

Let me analyze the key structural components of the GT:

1. **Term 1**: $c_0\epsilon^3$ — a cubic power of epsilon
2. **Term 2**: $c_2\epsilon^{0.266}\exp(-c_4/(c_5 T))$ — a fractional power of epsilon times an Arrhenius-type exponential in T
3. **Term 3**: $c_6\epsilon\sin(T - c_7)$ — epsilon times a sinusoidal function of T

The critical feature is **Term 2**, which contains $\exp(-\text{const}/T)$, an Arrhenius-type dependence on T. This is a very specific functional form in T.

Let me check each candidate for the ability to reproduce this $\exp(-1/T)$ dependence:

- Most candidates use terms like $\exp(c \cdot \epsilon)$, $\cos(T + c)$, $\log(\cdot)$, polynomial powers of $\epsilon$, etc. None of these can produce $\exp(-\text{const}/T)$.

- **Candidate 18**: Has $T \cdot c_0/(T \cdot c_1 + c_2)$ and $c_8/(T \cdot c_1 + c_2)$, which gives rational functions of T, not $\exp(-1/T)$.

- **Candidate 22**: Has $c_3\exp(T \cdot c_4)$, which is $\exp(\text{const} \cdot T)$, not $\exp(-\text{const}/T)$.

- **Candidate 30**: Has $c_4\exp(T \cdot c_5)$, same issue.

- **Candidate 43**: Has $c_3\exp(T \cdot c_4)$, same issue.

- **Candidate 37**: Has $T^{c_0} \cdot c_1$, a power law in T, not an Arrhenius form.

- **Candidate 36**: Has $c_0\epsilon^2 + c_1\epsilon^{1/4} + c_2\epsilon^{c_3} + c_4\epsilon + c_5 + c_6\epsilon\cos(T+c_7)$. The $\epsilon^{c_3}$ term could match $\epsilon^{0.266}$ and $\epsilon^3$, but there's no $\exp(-1/T)$ term. The T-dependence only comes through $\cos(T+c)$, not $\exp(-1/T)$.

- **Candidate 15**: Similar to 36, has $\epsilon^{c_3}$ but no exponential in T.

No candidate contains a term of the form $\exp(-\text{const}/T)$ or any equivalent that could produce Arrhenius-type temperature dependence. The $\epsilon^{0.266}\exp(-c/T)$ term in the GT couples epsilon and T in a way that none of the candidates can replicate. 

The candidates that have T-dependence only have it through $\cos(T+c)$, $\sin(T+c)$, $\exp(cT)$, $T^c$, or rational functions of T — none of which can equal $\exp(-\text{const}/T)$ for all T.

Furthermore, the GT has $\epsilon^3$ which requires either an explicit $\epsilon^2$ or $\epsilon^3$ term (or a flexible $\epsilon^{c}$ with $c=3$). Many candidates lack this capability, but even those with $\epsilon^{c}$ (candidates 15, 36, 49) still lack the Arrhenius T-dependence.

Therefore, no candidate can be made equivalent to the GT.

Conclusion: No match

The GT has three terms:
1. `c0*epsilon**3` — a cubic polynomial in epsilon
2. `c2*epsilon**c3*exp(-c4/(c5*T))` — a fractional power of epsilon times a Boltzmann-like exponential in T
3. `epsilon*c6*sin(T - c7)` — epsilon times a sinusoidal function of T

Key structural features:
- **epsilon**3 term** (cubic in epsilon)
- **exp(-const/T)** dependence on T (Arrhenius-type)
- **epsilon*sin(T + phase)** term (note: sin(T - c7) = sin(T + const) with appropriate phase shift, and epsilon*sin(T+c) can be written as epsilon*cos(T+c') with phase shift)

The sin term: `epsilon*sin(T - c7)` can be rewritten as `epsilon*cos(T + c2)` with appropriate c2, so `epsilon*cos(T + c2)` matches this basis function.

Now, the critical question for each candidate: does it contain the right **basis functions**?

The GT requires:
- **epsilon**3** (or equivalent polynomial)
- **exp(-const/T)** — this is NOT the same as exp(c*epsilon) or exp(c*T). The function exp(-a/T) cannot be represented by exp(b*epsilon), exp(c*T), log terms, polynomial terms, etc.

This is the key discriminator. Almost all candidates use `exp(c*epsilon)` instead of `exp(-c/T)`. The function `exp(-a/T)` is fundamentally different from `exp(b*epsilon)` — they depend on different variables and have completely different functional forms.

Let me check which candidates have an `exp(-const/T)` or equivalent term:

Going through all candidates, I see that virtually all use `exp(c*epsilon)` or `exp(c*T)`, NOT `exp(c/T)`. None of the candidates contain a term like `exp(c/T)` or any rational function of T inside an exponential.

Let me verify each candidate for the exp(-c/T) structure:

- Candidates 1-50: I'll scan for any that have `exp(something/T)` or `exp(c/T)`.

Looking carefully: None of the candidates have `exp(c/T)` or `exp(-c/T)`. They all have `exp(c*epsilon)`, `exp(c*T)`, or similar.

The function `exp(-c4/(c5*T))` is a fundamentally different basis function from anything available in any candidate. It cannot be replicated by `exp(c*epsilon)`, `exp(c*T)`, polynomials, logs, or trigonometric functions. By the principle of linear independence of basis functions, no candidate can match.

Let me also check candidates with `T**c0` (like Candidate 37: `T**c0*c1`). This is a power law in T, not exp(-c/T). These are linearly independent functions.

Candidate 18 has `T*c0/(T*c1 + c2)` — this is a rational function of T, not exp(-c/T).

No candidate contains the essential `exp(-const/T)` Arrhenius-type term.

Therefore, **no candidate matches the GT**.
